- The opponent's second move was rock.
- The opponent reverted to scissors on the third move and remained with scissors on the fourth move.
- On the fifth move, the opponent switched to paper.

The opponent's sequence of plays is: scissors, rock, scissors, scissors, paper.

1. The opponent is cycling through the moves in a non-standard order: perhaps scissors, rock, then a couple of scissors, followed by paper. 
2. The opponent's moves might be somewhat randomized but with a tendency towards using scissors more frequently (3 out of 5 rounds). 
3. There may be no easily discernible fixed pattern, but there's an observed preference for scissors, then a switch to paper.

Given the pattern so far, a defensive strategy that anticipates more instances of scissors could be beneficial, then to prepare for a potential random selection, covering less predictable plays like rock or paper.

     - Paper-Scissors: -1 (3 times)
     - Paper-Paper: +0 (3 times)

     - Scissors-Paper: +3 (3 times)
     - Scissors-Rock: -1 (4 times)
     - Scissors-Scissors: +0 (1 time)
   - Reward: Positive against 'paper', negative against 'rock'.

- The opponent sometimes plays the same move consecutively and seems to have some dependency on the previous few rounds' outcomes.
- Opponent often chooses rock after I choose scissors, suggesting a reactionary play towards my last choice.
- When I play 'paper', the opponent sometimes follows with 'scissors', especially after playing 'rock' prior.

To form a hypothesis about my opponent's strategy, let's look at the observed patterns in their plays and the corresponding rewards I received.

1. **Pattern Observation**:
    - The opponent seems to follow a sequence or a cyclic pattern where they frequently play scissors following my paper.
    - My losses mostly occur when I play paper, and the opponent often counters it with scissors.
    - There are several instances where I lose when playing rock against their paper.

2. **Reward Analysis for My Plays**:
    - **Rock**: Played 11 times; won 3 times against scissors, drew twice, lost 6 times mostly to paper.
    - **Paper**: Played 12 times; won 2 times both against rock, lost 10 times mostly to scissors.
    - **Scissors**: Played 20 times; won 4 times mostly against paper, drew once, lost 15 times mostly to rock.

3. **Opponent's Likely Strategy**:
    - They often play scissors after my paper and rock after my scissors.
    - The opponent seems to favor playing scissors and rock based on the frequency and pattern observed.
    - Their strategy could be a cyclic pattern or simply favoring rock and scissors over paper.

4. **Interpretation**:
